<text>Had very poor experience when we stopped as part of a bus tour.  Sonoma Cheese Factory has a ridiculous system of ordering.  You have to go to front, wait in line and place your order. Then you have to go to back, wait in line AGAIN and pay for your order.  THEN you have to go back up front and WAIT AGAIN for your order.
After placing my order and paying and waiting up front for 25 minutes for my sandwich I asked what was taking so long and got a curt reply.  After waiting another 10 minutes I asked again as out tour bus lunch stop was for 45 minutes and the employee was again unhelpful.  After complaining a THIRD TIME I was treated rudely so I requested a refund.  I was then told to go to the back and had to WAIT AGAIN for the manager who issued a refund without an apology.
I had to continue on the tour without a decent meal and barely made it back to the bus on time.
This delay prevented our ability to explore and shop in Sonoma and should not have happened
My recommendation is to eat elsewhere especially if you have less than an hour to waste.

< Review>
The Sonoma Cheese Factory was one of the stops on a tour we took while visiting San Francisco.  It was a large establishment with indoor and outdoor seating, wine tasting, restaurant for sandwiches, outside barbeque area to order food and a cheese display case that seemed like a mile long.  Best if all, free samples of the cheese.  And even better, all the free samples you could eat.  I believe we tried around 30 to  35 different flavors of Cheese.  pricing was par for course on cheeses and they had some great bundles as well.  We only left with two cheese but are looking forward to ordering more online.

We also tried ordering lunch from their sandwich shop and found it to be a tedious job.  Confussion on where to order, where the line to order was at and where to pick your food up at .  The food was decent enough, a bit pricey and took a long time to get after you ordered.< /Review>

<Rate>2</Rate><Review>The second star is for the various, well-protected cheese samples. The Lavender Cheddar was a particular favorite of mine.

Now for the missing stars. First up, so many flies. They had all the door wide open, which meant that the customers were just bombarded with flies as they walked around. I didn't want to order a sandwich here because of the issue, but my family was eating there, so I sucked it up.

I got the Sonoma deli sandwich. It was just okay. There was a lot of mustard, which overwhelmed the overall flavor of everything else in the sandwich.

Lastly, we sat in the indoor café area to eat. While there, I witnessed 10 customers walk up to the café counter, many of whom looked like they wished to order, but there was no employee present. They missed all of those sales because the employees kept wandering out to the patio or around to the front.

Overall, I understand that we were there on a Thursday, which may not be the busiest day of the week and was reflected in staffing levels, but the overall atmosphere and service quality of this establishment was very disappointing. < text>
I love that there is more than just cheese here!
I got a really good tri tip sandwich here. The meat was tender and the BBQ sauce was a prefect fit for the sandwich. The also have wine tasting here. We got a bottle and sat outside and drank it while we enjoyed lunch.
This is a lot more than just a cheese shop. They have fudge, ice cream or gelato (I can't remember which), and a lot of wines and wine accessories. It's a fun shop to stop in and grab a lunch to go or to dine at while you're out and about in Sonoma.< /text>

<userid>100131062883481326858</userid>< user_name>
Norm Gunn< /user_name>
< Time>
1410057205183<//Time>
<Rating>2< /Rating>< Text>
BAD DONUTS, high prices, beautiful decor, good service.

I was taken in by this place appearing on so many "best donuts in the Bay Area" lists.  I was also going to say I was taken in by Yelp reviews, but now looking back at them again I see that what I needed to know was already here.

Zagat rates restaurants from 1 to 30 on three independent scales:  food, decor, and service.  We're used to donut shops being in the single digits for decor and service, so someplace as "designed" as Doughnut Dolly is a standout for a donut shop -- it really is beautiful, and I love details like the folded napkins tucked between the donuts.  And the service, I have to say, is helpful and friendly.

But the donuts!  They're terrible!  They tasted stale and felt chewy -- and in a bad way,  like the old crust of something that used to be light.   The texture is more like two-week-old sourdough bread.  Then the fillings pumped into them are nothing like as tasty as the fans keep writing -- the mexican chocolate was fine, the best of them on my day, but even it was bland -- and it's pumped in super unevenly, so most of this small, weird-texture donut has no filling at all (and thus is unopposed badness), and the rest is overfilled and gross.  And the cherry filling, which is another one I had today, is overpoweringly sweet and gross.  Disgusting.  I couldn't eat it, and I was really looking forward to these donuts.

I just spent $9 for three small, bad donuts.  But at least I learned a lesson ... which is ... go to Johnnie's in Lafayette (the chocolate bar is best, and they'll fill it for you on the spot -- evenly! -- if you like), or Colonial Donuts in Oakland (get the blueberry donut, the buttermilk bar, or the apple fritter), or Bob's Donuts in San Francisco (try the crumb donut, their apple fritter is good but overrated -- and the glazed old fashioned sets the Bay Area's standard).</Text>

- tasty, fluffy doughnut
- rich, yet light, cream
- cute shop

Cons:
- the "naughty cream" in my doughnut was grainy and tasted a little off

<user>103379264202553362035</user><rate>2</rate><GmapID>0x80857de10dcd5381:0xa28c5aa68be0e0de</GmapID>< text>
Ahh, first the disappointment at Curbside, then the disappointment here. Continuing my fatassery, I stopped by Doughnut Dolly and got a naughty cream and dark chocolate to go, because I was way too full to eat them then and there. Except, well, I ate one of them ten minutes later, oops.

While the fillings themselves were quite tasty, the actual doughnut was fairly lacking: a little too dense and doughy for my tastes, with none of the light fluffiness I've come to love about a good raised doughnut. Thinking that throwing them into a toaster oven may help after trying the first doughnut, I only noticed marginal improvement with the second one I ate, to my dismay.

For those who do choose to come here though, the way it works is this: first you choose plain, powdered, or granulated sugar for your doughnut, and then you choose from four different flavor fillings, or combinations thereof, some of which rotate out. Pony up the ~$3 price tag, and you're set to go!

***Accessibility Info***

Venue - A small shop with your typical high ice cream display cases. Be prepared to reach a little ways up to get your sample spoons! Otherwise, since the venue is somewhat of an open-air layout, maneuverability isn't really an issue.

Bathroom - I don't believe I saw any public ones.</text>

105808225204845973594<//user_id>
<Text>I like living in Costa Verde! I've been here about a year now and have had only positive experiences.

I live in a one bedroom and the unit itself is big and has a lot of amenities that other apartments in this area do not have for the price. It is very affordable for how big it is and especially for having Full-Size Washer/Dryer in unit. I looked at a lot of apartments in this area and any apartment I found with W/D and a decent size was significantly more expensive.

The maintenance here is amazing. You put in a request online and Kevin, the maintenance coordinator, has always responded very quickly which I very much appreciate. You can either set up an appointment or give them permission to enter your unit. I usually give them permission to enter since I am at work during the weekdays. My problem has always been resolved within hours of reporting it. They always leave my place just as they found it too. Omar was the most recent technician to come to my apartment and he was awesome. He fixed the issue with my sink and put everything back the way he found it when he was done. Thank you!

Brad was the leasing agent that helped me from the beginning and he was super helpful. He answered all of my questions and guided me through the process, making it very easy and smooth (even at the start of Covid when everything was beginning to change and nobody had time to adjust yet). Everyone I have come across at the leasing office has been kind and helpful.

Receiving mail & packages here is safe as well. If you receive a package, it is left in a Parcel. They text you a code and you pick it up. As on online shopper, this is great!

My only complaint is the noise but that is inevitable. That is just part of living in an apartment, not specific to Costa Verde. I can definitely hear both my upstairs neighbors and the ones next to me, but again, that's just part of living in an apartment.

It's also very beautiful to walk around. Overall, I definitely recommend living in Costa Verde if you are looking in this area. :)< /Text><Rating>5<//Rating>< Resp>

It is regrettable that I am not able to select zero stars for this “community”. Thankfully, I do not live in Costa Verde Village. I went through the application process for an apartment. I was approved, but my deposit was not refunded because the property managers failed to inform me that I had been approved in the first place.

The customer service and communication is absolutely insufferable. Getting anyone on the phone is like pulling teeth. If you have a question and would like a return call expect it to take at least “5-7 business days”.

I thank each person who took the time to write reviews of this community and how horrendous property management is. I read these reviews and experienced this absolute negligence and disregard. I would also like to point out that there is an entire Instagram account devoted to someone’s hatred of this community @costaverdevillage which I found to be enlightening as well.

To anyone even considering calling this “community” home, do your research. Read the reviews. Check out the hashtag #ihatecostaverdevillage on Instagram. It’s a real thing. And read the fine print. The business practices here are questionable at best. I will bite my $250 deposit in the hopes that they can use that money to clean their hallways.

Lastly, while I absolutely abhor this place and its property management team, I have to say Brad in the leasing office was very nice. Brad, leave Costa Verde for something better! They don’t deserve you.

And that concludes my Ted Talk. *drops mic*< /text>

< review>
Great location sandwiched between the 805 and 5 freeways and a stone’s throw away from a small shopping center and UTC mall. The apartments could use some upgrades, but they’re a good value for the asking rent, especially if you include the move in specials. Residents seem to be comprised of small families and college-aged students. Neighborhood is very safe. There’s some noise from the nearby navy airfield during the day but it’s not too bad. I worked with Brad in the leasing office and he was very nice and easy to deal with.< /review>

< Text>
COCKROACHES. This review is LONG overdue (and long in length, so prepare yourselves).  I hope you're reading this, fellow UCSD or other university students who are currently looking for apartments.  Save your money and sanity.  Pick somewhere else.  And as if to underscore my point, I am writing this review in my closet with headphones on, trying to block out the eardrum-piercing fire alarm in my front entryway that decided to go off for no reason.  It's been over an hour since i submitted an emergency maintenance request and I'm sure I'll be waiting longer.  The headphones aren't working.

If you drive by Costa Verde, you'll see that their signs advertise "Luxury Apartments".  While they certainly are priced accordingly, what I received in exchange for my money was nearly a month of dealing with a large cockroach infestation.  My roommates and I moved into a two bedroom unit in the Southern portion of the complex.  About a day in and we started noticing signs of cockroach activity.  We had JUST finished moving in; no mess of our making brought them there as we hadn't even eaten inside yet.  You'd think that they'd care enough to check the place as it changes ownership and do some basic cleaning, but apparently such attention is not included with your luxury apartment.  After maybe a week, the activity became much worse, and we began to find them in our bedroom, bathroom, living room, kitchen, basically everywhere (even the ceiling).  It turns out that there had been a brown banded cockroach infestation behind the fridge for YEARS.  I pulled back that thing and roach feces just coated the bottom back of it, and they all came scurrying out, leaving behind exoskeletons, egg sacs, and dead roaches.  I have NEVER lived in any place with roaches, and brown banded roaches in particular are bad for me, as I have respiratory issues that are exacerbated by their activity.  It took TWO trips by the exterminator to bring them down, and each one forced us to once again remove all our kitchen supplies and painstakingly bag them and make them airtight.  We couldn't cook for that time, so we had to eat out, making the situation more annoying and costly.  When I asked to have our first month's rent refunded due to our awful experience, I was flatly rejected.  I asked if it was usual at Costa Verde Village to move in and be greeted by a cockroach infestation.  "No! Of course not!".  Well then since I'm an exception, I believe it's perfectly reasonable to request a refund due to the disgusting nature of the issue.  But management insisted that their policy is to "deal with infestations quickly" and no refunds would be given (even after admitting such an oversight was rare).  I don't believe for a second that what I was asking for was unreasonable.  My roommates and I would be idiots to be alright with paying thousands of dollars for a "luxury apartment", only to be greeted by Cockroach Verde.

Also EXTREMELY IMPORTANT to note is the large presence of homeless individuals/addicts that congregate in Costa Verde Village/Center. Break ins and package thefts aren't uncommon, and some of those people are quite disturbing (several days ago a homeless man standing very near my unit asked me for money, and began to spout racist nonsense when I refused. Afterwards he began to make grunting noises for about 15 minutes and pacing outside our hall.  If this would frighten you, think twice)

AND GET THIS, Costa Verde management decided that, somehow, planning a power outage during FINALS WEEK when a huge portion of their tenants are students was a good idea.  You'd think that postponing it by a week was possible to help the students.  Guess not.

Overall, there are tons of better options that surround us for you to check out.  My friends who live there are satisfied with their accommodations and, more importantly, the sincere manner in which management resolves issues suffered by their tenants.  We'll be looking to move out of Costa to somewhere else if we can find a good deal.  Oh, and the fire alarm is still going off and no one's here :).  Good luck< /Text>

<review>Around the beginning of the year, our upstairs neighbors (probably newly moved) started creating noise disturbance. We tolerated it for a few days hoping it would stop. Then we started filing complaints through the website and phone because it had reached a point where we went without proper sleep for two weeks straight. They would wake us up 3-4 times a night. We are not even light sleepers, they were just that loud. We started getting headaches, couldn't concentrate on work, and basically suffered from constant lack of sleep. We even tried to move when our lease was about to end but due to COVID, it didn't work out.

How Costa Verde dealt with it: The first few complaints we made were ignored. Not even acknowledged. After a month or so, I finally called them. They kept telling me they can't do anything about the noise during the day. I had to explain them a dozen of times that even though I reported the issue during the day, I have only made complaints of noise during the quiet hours (even though the noise is unbearable during the day). Because we don't take devices into our bedroom at night, I had to report them to the dispatch center in the daytime. When you are being awaken from your sleep in the middle of the night, your basic instinct is to try falling asleep again, and not walk to the other room, open your device, access a complicated website, fill a detailed form, and lodge a complaint. The leasing office asked us to make complain exactly when the noise occurs. So I started making some during 12am, 3am, 5.30am. Nothing. The person upstairs is so loud, we could have heard them walking to the door if the dispatch ever worked upon our complaints. Nothing was done.

Then we get a big letter at home telling the same things AGAIN. 1. That "we are a multifamily housing and you are expected to tolerate some noise." Of course, we know that. We have lived here for almost four years! The walls are so thin here, we can hear conversations of our next-door neighbor. We only had to report when things got so bad. 2. That we can't do anything about noise during non-quiet hours. YES. we know that too. But the noise is 24/7. Yesterday was the first time I made a complaint for noise during the day because it went for 6 straight hours, my ceiling sprinklers were vibrating due to the noise, and I was afraid something scary was going to happen. 3. The leasing office asked us to record the sounds or call the dispatch to our house to hear the noise. As insulting and creepy as that was, I did that too. I have sound clips and videos. I also called the dispatch, they never came. They never worked upon the videos and audios we sent and audios and kept giving different guidelines to record them.

The last six months have been the most stressful months of our lives. I sometimes go to Starbucks to work despite having a full empty apartment. We have lived here for four years and dozens of other places and had never had to react this way. We are saddened that Costa Verde Village was not only unhelpful against a problem as serious as this, but kept pointing their fingers at us instead of taking any actions.

Now, it's been 13 days and they haven't even replied to our emails. Not once have they streamline their protocol or been compassionate and tried to solve the mental harassment we have been enduring for so long. The only option they have given us is to vacate the apartment, which we happily would have if it was easy. We spent our entire long weekend waking up in the middle of the night and at 6 am due to the noise. We have videos and other proofs but unfortunately, they do not make any difference. < Text>
This is based purely on my experience of dealing with the sales department while trying to make a rather large recent purchase. My wife was narrowing  her choices to purchase a bedroom set and had established contact with a manger who then put her in contact with a member of the sales department. This member was extremely helpful and spent a tremendous amount of time going over things and working with my wife to ensure she was happy with her purchase and to make sure her needs were met. They agreed on a day that the purchase would be made and finalized.

Wanting to see the set for myself, I walked into the showroom on another day and was met with another member of the sales department. I told this sales associate that my wife was already working with another member of their team but I wanted to look at some bedroom sets. I asked some basic questions and looked at the sets my wife wanted me to see. I thanked the sales member for their time and said I would arrive in a couple of days with my wife to hopefully finish the purchase. At that time I was told that I shouldn’t wait and that the bedroom set needed to be ordered that day. I was told if I waited the set we wanted may not be available anymore. I told her I would meet with my wife and return in a few days.

A few days passed and I returned to the store to finalize the purchase with my wife. We were met with the associate I had spoke with and I informed them I would be needing the original associate that had been working with my wife. That original associate showed up and while my wife finished up the details of the purchase, I found out that the associate that showed me the sets I looked at, was now telling the other supervisor or manager on the floor that they would be “Splitting the purchase”. I guess that ment they would be splitting the commission. This didn’t feel right to me since the original associate was the one who did most of the work and also was the one  initially referred to my wife by the manager.

My wife and I finished our purchase and I walked out of there feeling a little bad for the original associate. To be honest the more I thought of it, the more I was actually thinking of canceling the order. Just because it didn’t feel right and I felt like the value of me as a customer was deminished. That is was all about the sale. From the pressure of having to seal the deal the day I went in, to the day we did show to finalize and being told the commission would be split. It’s going to take a while to feel good about wanting to do future business there... Especially if that’s the way the sales team treats each other and their customers. There’s plenty  of business to go around for all the sales associates. And to squabble over a commission didn’t make me feel good as a customer.<//Text>
